Refutation of the Second Proof
Author's refutation of the second proof using two arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the second proof, including the critique of the equality premise and the reductio ad absurdum.

Core Idea
Essences differ in reality, so equality fails; if accepted, equality leads to absurdities.

The author now responds to the second proof. He first shows that the premise of complete equality is false because essences differ in their realities. Then he argues that even if the premises were accepted, they would lead to absurd consequences such as the Creator becoming a creature, which is impossible. Thus the proof is unsound.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic from 'ولقائل أن يقول' to the end, and the corresponding translation. Notice the two parts of the refutation.
The refutation begins with a potential objector's voice: 'ولقائل أن يقول'.
2
Identify the first refutation
The author argues that the premise of equality is false because equal things would require different concomitants, which is impossible. Find this argument.
3
Understand the alternative view
The author proposes that essences are different in themselves but share the property of being not dependent on others. This preserves partial equality without full equality.
4
Examine the reductio ad absurdum
The author then shows that even if the premises held, they would lead to the possibility of the Creator becoming a creature, which is impossible. Since that does not obtain, the premises cannot be accepted.
This is a classic argument by contradiction.
5
Synthesize the overall refutation
Combine the two strategies: (1) the premise of equality is false, and (2) even if true, it leads to absurdity. The proof is thus invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية : قالوا : لا يجوز أن يكون شيء من الذوات علة لذات أخرى . لأنا بينا في المسألة المتقدمة : أن الذوات بأسرها متساوية في الذاتية ، وأن الاختلاف ليس إلا بالصفات ، فلو كانت ذات علة لذات ، لكان كل ذات علة لكل ذات. فيلزم كون الذات المعينة علة لنفسها. ويلزم كون الذات المعلولة عامة للذات التي فرض كونها علة وكل ذلك محال . فيثبت أنه لا يجوز أن يكون شيء من الذوات علة لشيء منها . ولقائل أن يقول : هذا بناء على أن الذوات متساوية في كونها ذوات، ونحن قد بينا بالبرهان اليقيني أن ذلك باطل ، إذ لو كان الأمر كذلك ، لزم أن تكون الأشياء المتساوية ، يلزمها لوازم مختلفة. وذلك محال في العقول . أما لو قلنا : إنها في أنفسها مختلفة إلا أنها مع اختلافها في حقائقها متشاركة في كونها ذوات ، بمعنى أنها أمور غير تابعة في وجودها لغيرها ، فعلى هذا التقدير فقد حصلت أشياء مختلفة في الماهية ، مع أنها تكون مشتركة في بعض اللوازم . فثبت : أن الحق ما ذكرناه . وإذا كان الأمر كذلك فقط سقط كلامكم . وأيضا : فمدار هذه الحجة على مقدمتين : إحداهما : أن الذوات بأسرها متساوية في الذاتية . والثانية : أن الأشياء المتساوية وجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما يصح على الآخر . فنقول : إن كان الأمر كذلك كما ذكرتم ، فحينئذ يلزمكم جواز أن ينقلب الخالق مخلوقا والمخلوق خالقا والممكن واجبا والواجب ممكنا ، وحينئذ يبطل عليكم كل ما ذكرتموه . ولما لم يلزم هذا ، فكذا مهنا.
Second proof: They said: It is not permissible that any essence be a cause of another essence. Because we have shown in the previous issue that all essences are equal in essence-hood, and that difference is only through attributes. So if an essence were a cause of an essence, then every essence would be a cause of every essence. This would necessitate that a specific essence be a cause of itself, and that the caused essence be general to the essence supposed to be its cause, and all that is impossible. Thus it is established that it is not permissible that any essence be a cause of any other. And one may say: This is based on the idea that essences are equal in being essences. And we have already proven by certain demonstration that this is false, for if that were the case, then equal things would necessitate different concomitants, and that is intellectually impossible. But if we say that they are different in themselves, yet despite their differences in realities they share in being essences, meaning that they are things not dependent in their existence on others, then on this estimation we have obtained things different in quiddity while they share in some concomitants. Thus it is established that the truth is what we have mentioned. And if that is the case, your argument collapses. Moreover, this proof rests on two premises: One: all essences are equal in essence-hood. Two: things that are equal must have the same properties. We say: If that is the case as you mentioned, then it would necessitate for you the possibility of the Creator becoming a creature and the creature becoming a creator, the contingent becoming necessary and the necessary becoming contingent, and then all that you have mentioned is invalidated. And since this does not follow, so too here.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the second proof against intermediaries, which argues that no essence can be a cause of another because all essences are equal in essence-hood. The refutation points out that essences are not completely equal; they differ in reality but share the property of not being dependent. Moreover, if the premises were accepted, they would lead to absurd consequences such as the Creator becoming a creature. Since those consequences are impossible, the premises must be false. The author thus shows the proof is unsound.

Key Terms
ذوات
مساواة
لوازم
ماهية
مقدمتان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all essences are identical in every respect, leading to the conclusion that causation is impossible.
Correction: The author clarifies that essences are different in their realities but share only the property of being not dependent, not complete equality.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does the author derive from accepting the premises of the second proof?
A) Infinite regress of causes.
B) The Creator becoming a creature.
C) All essences becoming identical.
D) Essences losing their attributes.

Key Takeaway
The second proof fails because essences are not fully equal in all respects, and even if they were, the premises lead to the absurdity of the Creator becoming a creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed that because you and another person share humanity, you must necessarily agree on every matter? Where might this false equality lead you in your relationships, and how does this lesson correct that assumption?
?
The author shows that accepting a false premise can lead to absurdities like the Creator becoming a creature. Think of a belief you hold about God that you have not fully examined. If that belief leads to an absurd consequence (even subtly), are you willing to abandon it? What would that require of you?
?
This passage guards against a proof that would make God and creation equal in essence. In your daily life, do you treat the Creator as fundamentally different from His creation, or do you sometimes forget His transcendence? Commit to one specific way you will remind yourself of this difference today.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
The Third Proof: Only God Can Create the World
The author presents a conditional proof for a single creator and notes its contested premise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical chain of the third proof for a single creator and why it depends on the denial of secondary causality.

Core Idea
Only God can create, or else two agents would share one power.

This lesson presents the third argument for the unity of the Creator. The author builds a conditional chain to show that if the world is originated, its creator must be the greatest deity, and that deity must be omnipotent. He then demonstrates that supposing another creator leads to the absurdity of one object of power belonging to two agents. Finally, he reveals a critical condition: this proof only works if we reject all secondary causality—a premise most thinkers reject.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof and trace the chain
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how each 'then' (ف) builds on the previous step. Can you list the implications in order?
The chain: world agent originated → its creator is the greatest deity → that deity can create all possibles → can create this world.
2
Identify the absurdity
The author introduces a supposition: if another being could create this world, then one object of power would belong to two capable beings. Understand why this is impossible in Islamic theology.
This is the core of the proof: the impossibility of two agents having exactly the same power over the same thing.
3
Examine the condition
The author states that the proof is incomplete unless we accept that only God's power has any effect. Reflect on why this premise is necessary for the logical chain to hold.
Without it, one could say the world creator is not the ultimate cause—secondary causes exist.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إن فاعل العالم بتقدير كونه محدثاً ، فإنه يجب أن يكون الإله الأكبر الذي هو الخالق لخالق هذا العالم قادرا على خلقه وإيجاده ، وإذا ثبت ذلك فوجب أن يكون قادرا على كل الممكنات ، وإذا ثبت ذلك فوجب أن يكون قادرا على خلق هذا العالم ، وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول : لو فرضنا شيئا آخر يقدر على خلق هذا العالم ، لزم حصول مقدور واحد لقادرين وهو محال . فوجب أن يكون هذا الفرض محالا . واعلم : أن هذه الحجة لا تتم إلا إذا قلنا : إنه لا يؤثر شيء في وجود شيء إلا قدرة الله تعالى ، وأكثر أهل العالم ينازعون في هذا الباب.
The third proof: If the agent of the world is assumed to be originated, then it must be that the greatest deity who is the Creator of the creator of this world is able to create and bring it into existence. And if that is established, then it must be that He is able to all possible things. And if that is established, then it must be that He is able to create this world. And if that is established, we say: if we suppose something else that is able to create this world, then the occurrence of one object of power for two capable beings would follow, which is impossible. Therefore, this supposition must be impossible. And know: this proof is not complete unless we say that nothing has effect in the existence of anything except the power of Allah, and most of the people of the world dispute this matter.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof that the creator of the world must be a single deity, based on the impossibility of two agents having the same object of power. However, the author notes a crucial condition: the proof only works if we accept that nothing causes existence except God's power. Most philosophers and theologians reject this premise, as they allow secondary causality. Thus the proof is not universally convincing.

Key Terms
فاعل
إله أكبر
ممكنات
مقدور
قادران

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the third proof is universally valid and does not rely on any additional premise.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the proof is incomplete unless we accept that only God's power has any effect in existence—a premise rejected by most philosophers and theologians.

Checkpoint
What condition does the author state for the third proof to be valid?
A) The world must be originated.
B) Only God's power has any effect in existence.
C) There must be only one possible world.
D) The proof is valid without any condition.

Key Takeaway
The third proof for a single creator depends on the controversial denial of secondary causality, making it unconvincing to those who accept natural causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that nothing in your life—every success, every trial, every provision—happens except by God's direct power? Or do you secretly attribute outcomes to natural causes, other people, or your own efforts? How would your daily reliance on God change if you lived with this belief?
?
When you face a difficulty, do you turn to secondary means (medicine, money, people) as the real causes, or do you look directly to God as the only source of effectiveness? The proof challenges you to examine where your trust actually lies. Are you willing to audit your prayers this week and see if they reflect this premise?
?
The author admits that most people dispute the premise that only God's power creates. Which side are you on? If you are honest, what evidence from your own life supports or contradicts the idea that secondary causes are truly effective? Write down one situation where you recently witnessed what seemed like a 'natural' cause—and ask yourself if your explanation acknowledged God's sole agency or not.
